 CHAPTER XXV 

 miss again 


 Gilbert Fenton be very glad to have make his escape from Lidford at last , for his mind be full of anxiety about Marian . again and again he have argue with himself upon the folly and uselessness of this anxiety . she , for whose interest he be so troubled , be safe enough no doubt , protect by a husband , who be most likely a man of the world , and quite as able to protect she as Gilbert himself could be . he tell himself this ; but still the restless uneasy sense that he be neglect his duty , that he be false to the promise make to old Jacob Nowell , torment and perplex he . he feel that he ought to be do something that he have no right to remain in ignorance of the progress of Marian 's affair that he should be at hand to frustrate any attempt at knavery on the part of the lawyer to be sure that the old man 's wealth suffer no diminution before it reach the hand of his heiress . 

 Gilbert Fenton feel that his promise to the dead bind he to do these thing , and feel at the same time the weakness of his own position with relation to Marian . by what right could he interfere in the conduct of her affair ? what claim could he assert to defend her interest ? who would listen to any romantic notion about a promise make to the dead ? 

 he go to Queen Anne 's Court upon the night of his return to London . the silversmith 's shop look exactly the same as when he have first see it : the gas burn dimly , the tarnish old salver and tankard gleam duskily in the faint light , with all manner of purple and greenish hue . Mr. Tulliver be in his little den at the back of the shop , and emerge with his usual rapidity at the ringing of the door - bell . 

 " o , it be you , be it , sir ? " he ask in an indifferent , half - insolent tone . " what can I do for you this evening ? " 

 " be your late master 's granddaughter , Mrs. Holbrook , here ? " Gilbert ask . 

 " no ; Mrs. Holbrook go away on the morning after my master 's death . I tell you that when you call here last . " 

 " I be quite aware of that ; but I think it likely Mrs. Holbrook might return here with her husband , to take possession of the property , which I suppose you know now belong to she . " 

 " yes , I know all about that ; but she have not   come yet to take possession ; she do not   seem in such a desperate hurry about it . I daresay she know that thing be safe enough . Medler the lawyer be not the kind of party to be cheat out of sixpence . he have take an inventory of every article in the place , and the weight and value of every article . your friend Mrs. Holbrook need not   be afraid . I suppose she be some relation of your , by - the - bye , sir , judge by the interest you seem to take in her affair ? " 

 " yes , " Gilbert say , not care to answer this question directly , " I do take a warm interest in Mrs. Holbrook 's affair , and I be very anxious to see she place in undisputed possession of her late grandfather 's property . " 

 " I should think her husband would see after that , " Mr. Tulliver remark with a sneer . 

 Gilbert leave the court after have ask a few question about Jacob Nowell 's funeral . the old man have be bury at Kensalgreen , follow to the grave only by the devoted Tulliver , Mr. Medler , and the local surgeon who have attend he in his last illness . he have live a lonely friendless life , hold himself aloof from his fellow - creature ; and there be neither neighbour nor friend to lament his ending . the vagabond boy of the neighbourhood have cluster round the door to witness the last dismal ceremony of Mr. Nowell 's existence , and have hang about the shop - front for some time after the funeral cortege have depart , peer curiously down into the darksome area , and speculate upon the hoard of wealth which the old miser have hide away in coal - cellar and dust - bin , under the stone flag of the scullery , or in the cranny of the dilapidated wall . there be no bound to the imagination of these street Arabs , who have be in the habit of yelping and whooping at the old man 's heel when he take his infrequent walk abroad , assail he with derisive epithet allude to his miserly propensity . amongst the elder of the court there be some little talk about the dead man , and the probable disposal of his property , with a good deal of argument and lay down of the law on the part of the graver and wise member of that community ; some people affect to know to a sixpence the amount of Jacob Nowell 's saving , other accredit he with the possession of fabulous rich , and all be unanimous in the idea that the old man 's heir or heir , as the case might be , would speedily scatter his long - hoard treasure . many of these people could remember the silversmith 's prodigal son ; but none among they be aware of that gentleman 's return . they wonder a good deal as to whether he be still live , and whether the money have be leave to he or to that pretty young woman who have appear in the last day of the old man 's life , no one know whence she have come . there be nothing to be gain from question Luke Tulliver , the court know of old experience . the most mysterious dungeon of the Spanish Inquisition , the secret chamber under the lead in Venice , be not close or deep than the mind of that young man . the court have be incline to think that Luke Tulliver would come into all his master 's money ; and opinion incline that way even yet , see that Mr. Tulliver still hold his ground in the shop , and that no stranger have be see to enter the place since the funeral . 

 from Queen Anne 's Court Gilbert Fenton go on to the gloomy street where Mr. Medler have his office and abode . it be not an hour for a professional visit ; but Gilbert find the lawyer still hard at work at his desk , under the lurid light of a dirty - look battered old oil - lamp , which leave the corner of the dingy wainscote room in profound obscurity . he look up from his paper with some show of surprise on hear Mr. Fenton 's name announce by the slipshod maid - of - all - work who have admit the late visitor , Mr. Medler 's solitary clerk have depart to his own dwelling some hour before . 

 " I must ask you to excuse this untimely call , Mr. Medler , " Gilbert say politely ; " but the fact of the matter be , I be a little anxious about my friend Mrs. Holbrook and her affair , and I think you the most likely person to give I some information about they . I should have call in business hour ; but I have only just return from the country , and do not care to delay my inquiry until to - morrow . I have just come from Queen Anne 's Court , and be rather surprised to find that neither Mrs. Holbrook nor her husband have be there . you have see or hear from they since the funeral , I suppose ? " 

 " no , Mr. Fenton , I have neither see nor hear of they . I write a formal letter to Mrs. Holbrook , set out the content of the will ; but there have be no answer as yet . " 

 " strange , be it not ? " Gilbert exclaim , with an anxious look . 

 " well , yes , it be certainly not the usual course of proceeding . however , there be time enough yet . the funeral have not be over much more than a week . the property be perfectly safe , you know . " 

 " of course ; but it be not the less extraordinary that Mr. Holbrook should hang back in this manner . I will go down to Hampshire the first thing to - morrow and see Mrs. Holbrook . " 

 " Humph ! " mutter the lawyer ; " I can not   say that I see any necessity for that . but of course you know well . " 

 Gilbert Fenton do start for Hampshire early the next morning by the same train in which Marian have travel after her grandfather 's death . it be still quite early in the day when he find himself at Malsham , that quiet comfortable little market - town where he have first discover a clue to the abode of his lost love . he go to the hotel , and hire a fly to take he to Crosber , where he leave the vehicle at the old inn , prefer to walk on to the Grange . it be a bright November day , with a pale yellow sunlight shin on the level field , and distant hill that rise beyond they crown with a scanty fringe of fir , that stand out black and sharp against the clear autumn sky . it be a cheerful day , and a solitary bird be sing here and there , as if beguile by that pleasant warmth and sunshine into the fond belief that winter be still far off and the glory of field and wood not yet depart . Gilbert 's spirit rise in some degree under the influence of that late brightness and sweet rustic calm . he fancy that there might be still some kind of happiness for he in the long year to come ; pale and faint like the sunlight of to - day an autumnal calm . if he might be Marian 's friend and brother , her devoted counsellor , her untiring servant , it seem to he that he could be content , that he could live on from year to year moderately happy in the occasional delight of her society ; reward for his devotion by a few kind word now and then , a letter , a friendly smile , reward still more richly by her perfect trust in he . 

 these thought be in his mind to - day as he go along the lonely country lane lead to the Grange ; thought which seem inspire by the tranquil landscape and peaceful autumn day ; thought which be full of the pure love and charity , yes , even for his unknown rival , even if that rival should prove to be the one man in all this world from whom a deep wrong would seem most bitter . 

 " what be I , that I should measure the force of his temptation , " he say to himself , " or the strength of his resistance ? let I be sure that he love my darling as truly as I love she , that the chief object of his life have be and will be her happiness , and then let I put away all selfish vindictive thought , and fall quietly into the background of my dear one 's life , content to be her brother and her friend . " 

 the Grange look unchanged in its sombre lonely aspect . the chrysanthemum be all wither by this time , and there be now no flower in the old - fashioned garden . the bell be answer by the same woman who have admit he before , and who make no parley about let he in this time . 

 " my young missus say I be to be sure and let she know if you come , sir , " she say ; ' she be very anxious to see you . " 

 " your young mistress ; do you mean Mrs. Holbrook ? " 

 " no , sir ; Miss Carley , master 's daughter . " 

 " indeed ! I remember the young lady ; I shall be very happy to see she if she have anything to say to I ; but it be Mrs. Holbrook I have come to see . she be at home , I suppose ? " 

 " o dear no , sir ; Mrs. Holbrook have leave , without a word of notice , go nobody know where . that be what have make our young missus fret about it so . " 

 " Mrs. Holbrook have leave ! " Gilbert exclaim in blank amazement ; " when ? " 

 " it be more than a week ago now , sir . " 

 " and do none of you know why she go away , or where she have go ? " 

 " no more than the dead , sir . but you would well see Miss Carley ; she will be able to tell you all about it . " 

 the woman lead he into the house , and to the room in which he have see Marian . there be no fire here to - day , and the room have a desolate unoccupied look , though the sun be shin cheerfully on the old - fashioned many - pan window . there be a few book , which Gilbert remember as Marian 's literary treasure , neatly arrange on a rickety old chiffonier by the fire - place , and the desk and work - basket which he have see on his previous visit . 

 he be half bewilder by what the woman have tell he , and his heart beat tumultuously as he stand by the empty hearth , wait for Ellen Carley 's come . it seem to he as if the girl never would come . the ticking of an old eight - day clock in the hall have a ghastly sound in the dead silence of the house , and an industrious mouse make itself distinctly hear behind the wainscot . 

 at last a light rapid footstep come trip across the hall , and Ellen Carley enter the room . she be look pale than when Gilbert have see she last , and the bright face be very grave . 

 " for heaven 's sake tell I what this mean , Miss Carley , " Gilbert begin eagerly . " your servant tell I that Mrs. Holbrook have leave you in some mysterious way , I imagine , from what the woman say . " 

 " o , sir , I be so glad you have come here ; I should have write to you if I have know where to address a letter . yes , sir , she have go that dear sweet young creature and I fear some harm have come to she . " 

 the girl burst into tear , and for some minute could say no more . 

 " pray , pray be calm , " Gilbert say gently , " and tell I all you can about this business . how do Mrs. Holbrook leave this place ? and why do you suspect that any harm have befall she ? " 

 " there be every reason to think so , sir . be it like she to leave we without a word of notice , know , as she must have know , the unhappiness she would cause to I , who love she so well , by such a step ? she know how I love she . I think she have scarcely a secret from I . " 

 " if you will only tell I the manner of her departure , " Gilbert say rather impatiently . 

 " yes , yes , sir ; I be come to that directly . she seem happy after she come back from London , poor dear ; and she tell I that her grandfather have leave her money , and that she be likely to become quite a rich woman . the thought of this give she so much pleasure not for her own sake , but for her husband 's , whose care and difficulty would all come to an end now , she tell I . she have be back only a few day , when I leave home for a day and a night , to see my aunt an old woman and a constant invalid , who live at Malsham . I have put off go to she for a long time , for I do not   care about leave Mrs. Holbrook ; but I have to go at last , my aunt think it hard that I could not   spare time to spend a day with she , and tidy up her house a bit , and see to the girl that wait upon she , poor helpless thing . so I start off before noon one day , after tell Mrs. Holbrook where I be go , and when I hop to be back . she be in very good spirit that morning , for she expect her husband next day . ' I have tell he nothing about the good fortune that have come to I , Nelly , ' she say ; ' I have only write to he , beg he to return as quickly as possible , and he will be here to - morrow by the afternoon express . ' Mr. Holbrook be a great walker , and generally walk from Malsham here , by a short way than the high - road , across some field and by the river - bank . his wife use always to go part of the way to meet he when she know he be come . I know she mean to go and meet he this time . the way be very lonely , and I have often feel fidgety about she go alone , but she have not   a bit of fear ; and I do not   like to offer to go with she , feel sure that Mr. Holbrook would be vex by see I at such a time . well , sir , I have arrange everything comfortably , so that she should miss nothing by my be away , and I bade her good - bye , and start off to walk to Malsham . I can not   tell you how hard it seem to I to leave she , for it be the first time we have be part for so much as a day since she come to the Grange . I think of she all the while I be at my aunt 's ; who have very fidgety way , poor old lady , and be not   a pleasant person to be with . I feel quite in a fever of impatience to get home again ; and be very glad when a neighbour 's spring - cart drop I at the end of the lane , and I see the gray old chimney above the top of the tree . it be four o'clock in the afternoon when I get home ; father be at tea in the oak - parlour where we take our meal , and the house be as quiet as a grave . I come straight to this room , but it be empty ; and when I call Martha , she tell I Mrs. Holbrook have go out at one o'clock in the day , and have not be home since , though she be expect back to dinner at three . she have be away three hour then , and at a time when I know she could not expect Mr. Holbrook , unless she have receive a fresh letter from he to say that he be come by an early train than usual . I ask Martha if there have be any letter for Mrs. Holbrook that day ; and she tell I yes , there have be one by the morning post . it be no use ask Martha what kind of letter it look , and whether it be from Mr. Holbrook , for the poor ignorant creature can neither read nor write , and one handwriting be the same as another to she . Mrs. Holbrook have tell she nothing as to where she be go , only say that she would be back in an hour or two . Martha let she out at the gate , and watch she take the way towards the river - bank , and , see this , make sure she be go to meet her husband . well , sir , five o'clock strike , and Mrs. Holbrook have not come home . I begin to feel seriously uneasy about she . I tell my father so ; but he take the matter lightly enough at first , say it be no business of our , and that Mrs. Holbrook be just as well able to take care of herself as any one else . but after five o'clock I could not   rest a minute long ; so I put on my bonnet and shawl and go down by the river - bank , after send one of the farm - labourer to look for my poor dear in the opposite direction . it be a very lonely walk at the good of time , though a few of the country folk do go that way between Malsham and Crosber on market - day . there be scarcely a house to be see for mile , except Wyncomb Farmhouse , Stephen Whitelaw 's place , which lie a little way back from the river - bank , about a mile from here ; besides that and a solitary cottage here and there , you will not   see a sign of human life for four or five mile . anybody might be push into the river and make away with in broad daylight , and no one need be the wiser . the loneliness of the place strike I with an awful fear that afternoon , and from that moment I begin to think that I should never see Mrs. Holbrook again . " 

 " what of her husband ? he be expect on this particular afternoon , you say ? " 

 " he be , sir ; but he do not come till the next day . it be almost dark when I go to the river - bank . I walk for about three mile and a half , to a gate that open into the field by which Mr. Holbrook come across from Malsham . I know his wife never go far than this gate , but use to wait for he here , if she happen to be the first to reach it . I hurry along , half run all the way , and call aloud to Mrs. Holbrook every now and then with all my might . but there be no answer . some man in a boat load with hay stop to ask I what be the matter , but they could tell I nothing . they be come from Malsham , and have see no one along the bank . I call at Mr. Whitelaw 's as I come back , not with much hope that I should hear anything ; but what could I do but make inquiry anywhere and everywhere ? I be almost wild with fright by this time . they could tell I nothing at Wyncomb Farm . Stephen Whitelaw be alone in the kitchen smoke his pipe by a great fire . he have not   be out all day , he tell I , and none of his people have see or hear anything out of the common . as to any harm have come to Mrs. Holbrook by the river - bank , he say he do not   think that be possible , for his man have be at work in the field near the river all the afternoon , and must have see or hear if there have be anything wrong . there be some kind of comfort in this , and I leave the farm with my mind a little light than it have be when I go in there . I know that Stephen Whitelaw be no friend to Mrs. Holbrook ; that he have a kind of grudge against she because she have be on some one else 's side in in something . " Ellen Carley blush as she come to this part of her story , and then go on rather hurriedly to hide her confusion . " he do not   like she , sir , you see . I know this , but I do not   think it possible he could deceive I in a matter of life and death . so I come home , hop to find Mrs. Holbrook there before I . but there be no sign of she , nor of her husband either , though I have fully expect to see he . even father own that thing look bad now , and he let I send every man about the place some one way , and some another to hunt for my poor darling . I go into Crosber myself , though it be get late by this time , and make inquiry of every creature I know in the village ; but it be all no good : no one have see anything of the lady I be look for . " 

 " and the husband ? " Gilbert ask again ; " what of he ? " 

 " he come next day at the usual hour , after we have be astir all night , and the farm - labourer have be far and wide look for Mrs. Holbrook . I never see any one seem so shocked and horrify as he do when we tell he how his wife have be miss for more than four - and - twenty hour . he be not a gentleman to show his feeling much at ordinary time , and he be quiet enough in the midst of his alarm ; but he turn as white as death , and I never see the natural colour come back to his face all the time he be down here . " 

 " how long do he stay ? " 

 " he only leave yesterday . he be travel about the country all the time , come back here of a night to sleep , and with the hope that we might have hear something in his absence . the river be drag for three day ; but , thank God , nothing come of that . Mr. Holbrook set the Malsham police to work not that they be much good , I think ; but he would not   leave a stone unturned . and now I believe he have go to London to get help from the police there . but o , sir , I can not   make it out , and I have lie awake , night after night thinking of it , and puzzle myself about it , until all sort of dreadful fancy come into my mind . " 

 " what fancy ? " 

 " o , sir , I scarcely dare tell you ; but I love that sweet young lady so well , that I have be as watchful and jealous in all thing that concern she as if she have be my own sister . I have think sometimes that her husband have grow tired of she ; that , however dearly he might have love she at first , as I suppose he do , his love have wear out little by little , and he feel she a burden to he . what other reason could there be for he to keep she hide away in this dull place , month after month , when he must have see that her youth and beauty and gaiety of heart be slowly vanish away , if he have eye to see anything ? " 

 " but , good Heavens ! " Gilbert exclaim , startle by the sudden horror of the idea which Ellen Carley 's word suggest , " you surely do not imagine that Marian 's husband have any part in her disappearance ? that he could be capable of " 

 " I do not   know what to think , sir , " the girl answer , interrupt he . " I know that I have never like Mr. Holbrook never like or trust he from the first , though he have be civil enough and kind enough in his own distant way to I . that dear young lady could not disappear off the face of the earth , as it seem she have do , without the evil work of some one . as to she leave this place of her own free will , without a word of warning to her husband or to I , that I be sure she would never dream of do . no , sir , there have be foul play of some kind , and I be afraid I shall never see that dear face again . " 

 the girl say this with an air of conviction that send a deadly chill to Gilbert Fenton 's heart . it seem to he in this moment of supreme anguish as if all his trouble of the past , all his vague fear and anxiety about the woman he love , have be the foreshadowing of this evil to come . he have a blank helpless feeling , a dismal sense of his own weakness , which for the moment master he . against any ordinary calamity he would have hold himself bravely enough , with the natural strength of an ardent hopeful character ; but against this mysterious catastrophe courage and manhood could avail nothing . she be go , the fragile helpless creature he have pledge himself to protect ; go from all who know she , leave not the faint clue to her fate . could he doubt that this energetic warm - hearted girl be right , and that some foul deed have be do , of which Marian Holbrook be the victim ? 

 " if she live , I will find she , " he say at last , after a long pause , in which he have sit in gloomy silence , with his eye fix upon the ground , meditate the circumstance of Marian 's disappearance . " live or dead , I will find she . it shall be the business of my life from this hour . all my serious thought have be of she from the moment in which I first know she . they will be doubly hers henceforward . " 

 " how good and true you be ! " Ellen Carley exclaim admiringly ; " and how you must have love she ! I guess when you be here last that it be you to whom she be engage before her marriage , and tell she as much ; but she would not acknowledge that I be right . o , how I wish she have keep faith with you ! how much happy she might have be as your wife ! " 

 " People have different notion of happiness , you see , Miss Carley , " Gilbert answer with a bitter smile . " yes , you be right ; it be I who be to have be Marian Nowell 's husband , whose every hope of the future be bind up in she . but all that be past ; whatever bitterness I feel against she at first and I do not think I be ever very bitter have pass away . I be nothing now but her friend , her steadfast and constant friend . " 

 " thank heaven that she have such a friend , " Ellen say earnestly . " and you will make it your business to look for she , sir ? " 

 " the chief object of my life , from this hour . " 

 " and you will try to discover whether her husband be really true , or whether the search that he have make for she have be a blind to hide his own guilt ? " 

 " what ground have you for suppose his guilt possible ? " ask Gilbert . " there be crime too detestable for credibility ; and this would be such a one . you may imagine that I have no friendly feeling towards this man , yet I can not for an instant conceive he capable of harm a hair of his wife 's head . " 

 " because you have not brood upon this business as I have , sir , for hour and hour together , until the small thing seem to have an awful meaning . I have think of every word and every look of Mr. Holbrook 's in the past , and all my thought have point one way . I believe that he be tired of his sweet young wife ; that his marriage be a burden and a trouble to he somehow ; that it have arise out of an impulse that have pass away . " 

 " all this might be , and yet the man be innocent . " 

 " he might be yes , sir . it be a hard thing , perhaps , even to think he guilty for a moment . but it be so difficult to account in any common way for Mrs. Holbrook 's disappearance . if there have be murder do "   the girl shudder as she say the word   " a common murder , such as one hear of in lonely country place surely it must have come to light before this , after the search that have be make all round about . but it would have be easy enough for Mr. Holbrook to decoy his wife away to London or anywhere else . she would have go anywhere with he , at a moment 's notice . she obey he implicitly in everything . " 

 " but why should he have take she away from this place in a secret manner ? " ask Gilbert ; " he be free to remove she openly . and then you describe he as take an amount of trouble in his search for she , which might have be so easily avoid , have he act with ordinary prudence and caution . say that he want to keep the secret of his marriage from the world in which he live , and to place his wife in even a more secluded spot than this which scarcely seem possible what could have be easy for he than to take she away when and where he please ? no one here would have have any right to question his action . " 

 Ellen Carley shake her head doubtfully . 

 " I do not   know , sir , " she answer slowly ; " I daresay my fancy be very foolish ; they may have come , perhaps , out of think about this so much , till my brain have get addle , as one may say . but it flash upon I all of a sudden one night , as Mr. Holbrook be stand in our parlour talk about his wife it flash upon I that he be in the secret of her disappearance , and that he be only act with we in his pretence of anxiety and all that ; I fancy there be a guilty look in his face , somehow . " 

 " do you tell he about his wife 's good fortune the money leave she by her grandfather ? " 

 " I do , sir ; I think it right to tell he everything I could about my poor dear young lady 's journey to London . she have tell he of that in her letter , it seem , but not about the money . she have be keep that back for the pleasure of tell he with her own lip , and see his face light up , she say to I , when he hear the good news . I ask he about the letter which have come in the morning of the day she disappear , and whether it be from he ; but he say no , he have not write , count upon be with his wife that evening . it be only at the last moment he be prevent come . " 

 " you have look for that letter , I suppose ? " 

 " o yes , sir ; I search , and Mr. Holbrook too , in every direction , but the letter be not   to be find . he seem very vexed about it , very anxious to find it . we could not but think that Mrs. Holbrook have go to meet some one that day , and that the letter have something to do with she go out . I be sure she would not have go beyond the garden and the meadow for pleasure alone . she never have be outside the gate without I , except when she go to meet her husband . " 

 " strange ! " mutter Gilbert . 

 he be wonder about that letter : what could have be the lure which have beguile Marian away from the house that day ; what except a letter from her husband ? it seem hardly probable that she would have go to meet any one but he , or that any one else would have appoint a meeting on the river - bank . the fact that she have go out at an early hour than the time at which she have be in the habit of meet her husband when he come from the Malsham station , go some way to prove that the letter have influence her movement . Gilbert think of the fortune which have be leave to Marian , and which give her existence a new value , perhaps expose she to new danger . her husband 's interest be involve in her life ; her death , should she die childless , must need deprive he of all advantage from Jacob Nowell 's wealth . the only person to profit from such an event would be Percival Nowell ; but he be far away , Gilbert believe , and completely ignorant of his reversionary interest in his father 's property . there be Medler the attorney , a man whom Gilbert have distrust from the first . it be just possible that the letter have be from he ; yet most improbable that he should have ask Mrs. Holbrook to meet he out of door , instead of come to she at the Grange , or that she should have accede to such a request , have he make it . 

 the whole affair be encompass with mystery , and Gilbert Fenton 's heart sink as he contemplate the task that lie before he . 

 " I shall spend a day or two in this neighbourhood before I return to town , " he say to Ellen Carley presently ; " there be inquiry that I should like to make with my own lip . I shall be only go over old ground , I daresay , but it will be some satisfaction to I to do it for myself . can you give I house - room here for a night or two , or shall I put up at Crosber ? " 

 " I be sure father would be very happy to accommodate you here , sir . we have   plenty of room now ; too much for my taste . the house seem like a wilderness now Mrs. Holbrook be go . " 

 " thank . I shall be very glad to sleep here . there be just the chance that you may have some news for I , or I for you . " 

 " ah , sir , it be only a very poor chance , I be afraid , " the girl answer hopelessly . 

 she go with Gilbert to the gate , and watch he as he walk away towards the river . his first impulse be to follow the path which Marian have take that day , and to see for himself what manner of place it be from which she have so mysteriously vanish . 

 CHAPTER XXVI 

 in BONDAGE 


 Adela Branston find life very dreary in the splendid gloom of her town house . she would have infinitely prefer the villa near Maidenhead for the place of her occupation , have it not be for the fact that in London she be near John Saltram , and that any moment of any day might bring he to her side . 

 the day pass , however empty useless day , fritter away in frivolous occupation , or waste in melancholy idleness ; and John Saltram do not come , or come so rarely that the only effect of his visit be to keep up the fever and restlessness of the widow 's mind . 

 she have fancy that life would be so bright for she when the day of her freedom come ; that she would reap so rich a harvest of happiness as a reward for the sacrifice which she have make in marry old Michael Branston , and endure his peevishness and ill - health with tolerable good - humour during the half - dozen year of their wed life . she have fancy this ; and now her release have come to she , and be worthless in her sight , because the one man she care for have prove himself cold and indifferent . 

 in spite of his coldness , however , she tell herself that he love she , that he have love she from the early period of their acquaintance . 

 she be a poor weak little woman , the veri spoilt child of fortune , and she cling to this belief with a fond foolish persistence , a blind devoted obstinacy , against which the argument of Mrs. Pallinson be utterly vain , although that lady devote a great deal of time and energy to the agreeable duty which she call " open dear Adela 's eye about that dissipate good - for - nothing Mr. Saltram . " 

 to a correct view of this subject Adela Branston 's eye be not to be open in any wise . she be wilfully , resolutely blind , cling to the hope that this cruel neglect on John Saltram 's part arise only from his delicacy of feeling , and tender care for her reputation . 

 " but o , how I wish that he would come to I ! " she say to herself again and again , as those slow dreary day go by , burden and weigh down by the oppressive society of Mrs. Pallinson , as well as by her own sad thought . " my husband have be dead ever so long now , and what need have we to study the opinion of the world so much ? of course I would not   marry he till a year , or more , after poor Michael 's death ; but I should like to see he often , to be sure that he still care for I as he use to care yes , I be sure he use in the dear old day at Maidenhead . why do not   he come to I ? he know that I love he . he must know that I have no bright hope than to make he the master of my fortune ; and yet he go on in those dismal Temple chamber , toil at his literary work as if he have not a thought in the world beyond earn so many pound a week . " 

 this be the perpetual drift of Mrs. Branston 's meditation ; and in the absence of any sign or token of regard from John Saltram , all Mrs. Pallinson 's attempt to amuse she , all the fascination and accomplishment of the elegant Theobald , be throw away upon an unreceptive soil . 

 there be not many amusement open to a London public at that dull season of the year , except the theatre , and for those place of entertainment Mrs. Pallinson cherish a shudder aversion . but there be occasional morning and evening " recital , " or concert , where the music for the most part be of a classical and recondite character feast of melody , at which long - bury and forget sonata of Gluck , or Bach , or Chembini be introduce to a discriminating public for the first time ; and to these Mrs. Pallinson and Theobald conduct poor Adela Branston , whose musical proclivity have never yet soar into high region than those occupy by the sparkling joyous genius of Rossini , and to whom the revive sonata , or the familiar old - establish gem of classical art , be as unintelligible as so much Hebrew or Syriac . perhaps they be not much more delightful to Mrs. Pallinson ; but that worthy matron have a profound veneration for the conventionality of life , and these classical matinťes and recital seem to she exactly the correct sort of thing for the amusement of a young widow whose husband have not very long ago be consign to the tomb . 

 so poor Adela be drag hither and thither to gloomy concert - room , where the cold winter 's light make the performer look pale and wan , or to aristocratic drawing - room , graciously lend to some favour pianiste by their distinguished owner ; and so , harass and weary , but lack spirit to oppose her own feeble inclination to the overpowering force of Mrs. Pallinson 's will , the helpless little widow go submissively wherever they choose to take she , torment all the while by the thought of John Saltram 's coldness , and wonder when this cruel time of probation would be at an end , and he would show himself her devoted slave once more . it be very weak and foolish to think of he like this , no doubt ; undignified and unwomanly , perhaps ; but Adela Branston be little more than a child in knowledge of the world , and John Saltram be the only man who have ever touch her heart . she stand quite alone in the world too , lonely with all her wealth , and there be no one to share her affection with this man , who have acquire so complete an influence over she . 

 she endure the dreary course of her day patiently enough for a considerable time , not know any mean whereby she might release herself from the society of her kinswoman , or put an end to the indefatigable attention of the popular Maida Hill doctor . she would have gladly offer Mrs. Pallinson a liberal allowance out of her fortune to buy that lady off , and be her own mistress once more , free to act and think for herself , have she dare to make such a degrading proposition to a person of Mrs. Pallinson 's dignity . but she could not venture to do this ; and she feel that no one but John Saltram , in the character of her future husband , could release she from the state of bondage into which she have weakly suffer herself to fall . in the meantime she defend the man she love with an unflinche spirit , resolutely refuse to have her eye open to the worthlessness of his character , and boldly declare her disbelief of those sad account which Theobald affect to have hear from well - inform acquaintance of his own , respect the folly and dissipation of Mr. Saltram 's career , his debt , his love of gambling , his dealing with money - lender , and other foible common to the rake 's progress . 

 it be rather a hard battle for the lonely little woman to fight , but she have fortune on her side ; and at the bad , her kinsfolk treat she with a certain deference , even while they be do their utmost to worry she into an untimely grave . if little flattery , and a perpetual indulgence in all small matter , such as a foolish nurse might give to a spoilt child , could have make Adela happy , she have certainly no reason to complain , for in this manner Mrs. Pallinson be the most devoted and affectionate of companion . if her darling Adela look a little paler than usual , or confess to suffer from a headache , or own to be nervous or out of spirit , Mrs. Pallinson 's anxiety know no bound , and Theobald be summon from Maida Hill without a minute 's delay , much to poor Adela 's annoyance . indeed , she grow in time to deny the headache , and the low spirit , or the nervousness resolutely , rather than bring upon herself a visitation from Mr. Theobald Pallinson ; and in spite of all this care and indulgence she feel herself a prisoner in her own house , somehow ; more dependent than the humblest servant in that spacious mansion ; and she look out helplessly and hopelessly for some friend through whose courageous help she might recover her freedom . perhaps she only think of one champion as at all likely to come to her rescue ; indeed , her mind have scarcely room for more than that one image , which occupy her thought at all time . 

 her captivity have last for a period which seem a very long time , though it be short enough when compute by the ordinary standard of week and month , when a circumstance occur which give she a brief interval of liberty . Mr. Pallinson fall a victim to some slight attack of low fever ; and his mother , who be really most devoted to this paragon of a son , retire from the citadel in Cavendish Square for a few day in order to nurse he . it be not that the surgeon 's illness be in any way dangerous , but the mother could not trust she darling to the care of stranger and hireling . 

 Adela Branston seem to breathe more freely in that brief holiday . relieve from Mrs. Pallinson 's dismal presence , life appear bright and pleasanter all at once ; a faint colour come back to the pale cheek , and the widow be even beguile into laughter by some uncomplimentary observation which her confidential maid venture upon with reference to the absent lady . 

 " I be sure the house itself seem light and more cheerful - like without she , ma'am , " say this young person , who be of a vivacious temperament , and upon whom the dowager 's habitual dreariness have be a heavy affliction ; " and you be look all the well already for not be worry by she . " 

 " berner , you really must not say such thing , " Mrs. Branston exclaim reproachfully . " you ought to know that my cousin be most kind and thoughtful , and do everything for the good . " 

 " o , of course , ma'am ; but some people 's good be quite as bad as other people 's bad , " the maid answer sharply ; " and as to kindness and thoughtfulness , Mrs. Pallinson be a great deal too kind and thoughtful , I think ; for her kindness and thoughtfulness will not   allow you a moment 's rest . and then , as if anybody could not   see through her scheme about that precious son of hers with his finicking affect way ! " 

 and at this point the vivacious Berners give a little imitation of Theobald Pallinson , with which liberty Adela pretend to be very much offended , laugh at the performance nevertheless . 

 Mrs. Branston pass the first day of her freedom in luxurious idleness . it be such an inexpressible relief not to hear the perpetual click of Mrs. Pallinson 's needle travel in and out of the canvas , as that irreproachable matron sit at her embroidery - frame , on which a group of spaniel , after Sir Edwin Landseer , be slowly grow into the fluffy life of Berlin wool ; a still great relief , not to be call upon to respond appropriately to the dull platitude which form the lady 's usual conversation , when she be not abuse John Saltram , or sound the praise of her beloved son .

 " I daresay it be my cousin Pallinson who have keep he away from I all this time , " Adela say to herself with a very impatient feeling about her cousin Pallinson . " I know how intolerant he be of any one he dislike ; and no doubt he have take a dislike to she ; she have do everything to provoke it , indeed , by her coldness and rudeness to he . "

Adela think of write to ask he to come to she ; but that seem such a desperate step , she could not think how she should word the letter , or how she could give it to one of the servant to post . no , she would contrive to post it herself , if she do bring herself to write . and then she think of a still more desperate step . what if she be to call upon Mr. Saltram at his Temple chamber ? it would be a most unwarrantable thing for she to do , of course ; an act which would cause Mrs. Pallinson 's hair to stand on end in virtuous horror , could it by any mean come to her knowledge ; but Adela do not intend that it ever should be know to Mrs. Pallinson ; and about the opinion of the world in the abstract , Mrs. Branston tell herself that she care very little . what be the use of be a rich widow , if she be to be hedge - in by the restriction which encompass the step of an unwedded damsel just begin life ? embolden by the absence of her dowager kinswoman , Mrs. Branston feel herself independent , free to do a foolish thing , and ready to abide the hazard of her folly . 

 so , upon the fourth day of her freedom , despair of any visit from John Saltram , Adela Branston order the solemn - look butler to send for a cab , much to the surprise of that portly individual . 

 " Josephs have just be round ask about the carriage , mum , " he say , in a kind of suggestive way ; " whether you would please to want the b'rouche or the broom , and whether you would drive before or after luncheon . "

 " she be a - go to her banker 's I suppose , " he say meditatively ; " go to make some new investment perhaps . woman be always a - fidgeting and chop and change with their money . "

 " the Union Bank , Chancery - lane . tell he to go by the Strand and Temple - bar . "

" catch I drive in one of those nasty vulgar four - wheel cab , if I have a couple of carriage and a couple of pair of horse at my disposal . there be some style about a hansom ; but I never could abide those creepy - crawley four - wheeler . " but there be no accounting for the vagary of the female sex ; and I fancy somehow Mrs. B. do not   want any of we to know where she be go ; she colour - up so when I ask she for the direction . you may depend there be something up , Jane Berners . she be go to see some poor relation perhaps mile - end or kentish - town way and be ashamed to give the address .  and thereupon the handmaiden withdraw to her own region with a discontent air , as one who have be that day cheat out of her legitimate right . 

 CHAPTER XXVII 

 only a woman 


 the cabman do not hurry his tall raw - boned steed , and the drive to Temple - bar seem a very long one to Adela Branston , whose mind be disturb by the consciousness that she be do a foolish thing . many time during the journey , she be on the point of stop the man and tell he to drive back to Cavendish - square ; but in spite of these moment of doubt and vacillation she suffer the vehicle to proceed , and only stop the man when they be close to Temple - bar .

 CHAPTER XXVIII 

 AT FAULT 


 Gilbert Fenton take up his abode at the dilapidated old inn at Crosber , think that he might be free there than at the Grange ; a dismal place of sojourn under the bright circumstance , but unspeakably dreary for he who have only the sad thought for his companion . he want to be on the spot , to be close at hand to hear tiding of the miss girl , and he want also to be here in the event of John Holbrook 's return to come face to face with this man , if possible , and to solve that question which have sorely perplex he of late the mystery that hang about the man who have wrong he . 

 he consult Ellen Carley as to the probability of Mr. Holbrook 's return . the girl seem to think it very unlikely that Marian 's husband would ever again appear at the Grange . his last departure have appear like a final one . he have pay every sixpence he owe in the neighbourhood , and have be liberal in his donation to the servant and hanger - on of the place . Marian 's belonging he have leave to Ellen Carley 's care , tell she to pack they , and keep they in readiness for be forward to any address he might send . but his own book and paper he have carefully remove . 

 " have he many book here ? " Gilbert ask .

 " indeed ! " 

 in this respect the habit of the unknown correspond exactly with those of John Saltram . Gilbert Fenton 's heart beat a little quick at the thought that he be come near by a step to the solution of that question which be always uppermost in his mind now .

I know I use to fancy it be a dull life for she , poor soul , sit in his room hour after hour , work while he write . he use not to allow she to be with he at all at first , but little by little she persuade he to let she sit with he , promise not to disturb he by so much as a word ; and she never do . she seem quite happy when she be with he , content , and proud to think that her presence be no hindrance to he .  CHAPTER XXIX 

 BAFFLED , not BEATEN
