 John Saltram , otherwise John Holbrook , be not destine to die upon this outward voyage . he be very eager to be well , or at least to be at liberty to move about again ; and perhaps this impatient desire of his help in some measure to bring about his recovery . the will , physiologist tell we , have a great deal to do with these thing . 

 the voyage be a prosperous one . the good ship steam gaily across the Atlantic through the bleak spring weather ; and there be plenty of eat and drink , and joviality and flirtation on board she , while John Saltram lie upon his back , very helpless , languish to be astir once more .

 " she be a hard one ! " the steward remark to the stewardess , when they talk the matter over in a comfortable manner during the progress of a snug little supper in the steward 's cabin , ' she must be an out - and - out hard - hearted one to stand out against he like that , if he be her husband , and I suppose he be . I tell she to - day when I take his message how bad he be , and that it be a chance if he ever go ashore alive ; but she be walk up and down deck with her father ten minute afterwards , laugh and talk like anything . "

I have be too ill to stir ever since I come on board , or you would have hear of I before this , Mr. Nowell . now that I can move about once more , I shall find a way to assert my claim , you may be sure . but in the first place , I want to know by what right you stole my wife away from her home by what right you bring she on this voyage ? " 

 " before I answer that question , Mr. Mr. Holbrook , as you choose to call yourself , I will ask you another . by what right do you call yourself my daughter 's husband ? what evidence have you to produce to prove that you be not a bare - faced impostor ? you do not   carry your marriage - certificate about with you , I daresay ; and in the absence of some kind of documentary evidence , what be to convince I that you be what you pretend to be my daughter 's husband ? "

" 

 it be hard for John Saltram to hear any man talk like this , and not be able to knock he down . but in his present condition Marian 's husband could not have grapple a child , and he know it .

 " hard word mean so little , " return Mr. Nowell coolly , " and go for so little . that kind of language before witness would be actionable ; but , upon my word , it would be mere child 's play on my part to notice it , especially to a man in your condition . you would well claim your wife from the captain , and see what he will say to you . I have tell he that there be some semi - lunatic on board , who pretend to be Mrs. Holbrook 's husband ; so he will be quite prepared to hear your statement . " 

 John Saltram leave the saloon in silence . it be bad than useless talk to this man , who presume upon his helpless state , and openly defy he . his next effort must be to see Marian . 

 this he find impossible , for the time be at any rate . the state - room number 7 be an apartment a little big than a rabbit - hutch , open out of a large cabin , and in that cabin there repose a ponderous matron who have suffer from sea - sickness throughout the voyage , and who could in no wise permit a masculine intruder to invade the scene of her retirement . 

 the idea of any blockade of Marian 's door be therefore futile . he must need wait as patiently as he might , till she appear of her own free will . he could not have to wait very long ; something less than a day and a night , the steward have tell he , would bring they to the end of the voyage .

 he have no idea of make his wrong know to the captain , unless as a last desperate resource . he could not bring himself to make Marian the subject of a vulgar squabble . no , it be to herself alone he would appeal ; it be in the natural instinct of her own heart that he would trust . 

 very long and weary seem the remain hour of that joyless voyage . Mr. Saltram be fain to go back to his cabin after an hour on deck , there to lie and await the morrow . he have need to husband his strength for the come encounter . the steward tell he in the evening that Mrs. Holbrook have not din in the saloon that day , as usual . she have keep her cabin closely , and complain of illness .

 Mr. Saltram , have duly deliberate the matter during the long hour of that weary night , have decide that his wise course be to lie perdu until the last moment , the very moment of landing , and then to come boldly forward and make his claim . it be useless to waste his strength in any futile endeavour to baffle so hardy a scoundrel as Percival Nowell . at the last , when Marian be leave the ship , it would be time for he to assert his right as her husband , and to defy the wretch who have beguile she away from he .

 she be closely veil , her face quite hide by thick black lace , and she be cling with something of a frightened air to her companion 's arm .

 " Marian , " he say , in slow decide tone , " let go that man 's arm . you will leave this vessel with I , and with no one else . " 

 " stand out of the way , fellow , " cry Percival Nowell ; " my daughter can have nothing to say to you . " 

 " Marian , for God 's sake , obey I ! there be the vile treachery in this man 's conduct . let go his arm . my love , my darling , come with I ! " 

 there be a passionate appeal in his tone , but it produce no answer . 

 " Marian ! " he cry , still interpose himself between these two and the passage to the landing wharf . " Marian , I will have some answer ! " 

 " you have have your answer , sir , " say Percival Nowell , try to push he aside . " this lady do not know you . do you want to make a scene , and render yourself ridiculous to every one here ? there be plenty of lunatic asylum in New York that will accommodate you , if you be determined to make yourself eligible for they . " 

 " marian ! " repeat John Saltram , without vouchsafe the faint notice of this speech . " Marian , speak to I ! " 

 and then , as there come no answer from that shrink clinging figure , with a sudden spring forward , that bring he quite close to she , John Saltram tear the veil away from the hidden face . 

 " this must be some impostor , " he say ; " this be not my wife . " 

 he be right . the creature cling to Percival Nowell 's arm be a pretty woman enough , with rather red hair , and a common face . she be about Marian 's height ; and that be the only likeness between they . 

 the spectator of this brief fracas crowd round the actor in it , see nothing but the insult offer to a lady , and highly indignant with John Saltram ; and amidst their murmur Percival Nowell push his way to the shore , with the woman still cling to his arm . 

 CHAPTER XLII

 that shrill anguish - stricken cry which Ellen Whitelaw have hear on the night of the stranger 's visit to Wyncomb Farm haunt she afterwards with a wearisome persistence . she could not forget that wild unearthly sound ; she could not help continually try to find some solution for the mystery , until her brain be tired with the perpetual effort .

 CHAPTER XLIII 

 MR . WHITELAW make an END of the MYSTERY 


 Mrs. Whitelaw have be marry about two month . it be bright May weather , bright but not yet warm ; and whatever prettiness Wyncomb Farm be capable of assume have be put on with the fresh spring green of the field and the young leaf of the poplar . there be even a few hardy flower in the vegetable - garden behind the house , humble perennial plant by dead and go Whitelaws , which have bloom year after year in spite of Stephen 's utilitarian principle . it be a market - day , the household work be finish , and Ellen be sit with Mrs. Tadman in the parlour , where those two spend so many weary hour of their life , the tedium whereof be relieve only by woman 's homely resource , needlework . even if Mrs. Whitelaw have be fond of reading , and she only care moderately for that form of occupation , she could hardly have find intellectual diversion of that kind at Wyncomb , where a family Bible , a few volume of the Annual Register , which have belong to some half - dozen different owner before they come from a stall in Malsham market to the house of Whitelaw , a grim - look old quarto upon domestic medicine , and a cookery - book , form the entire library . when the duty of the day be do , and the local weekly newspaper have be read an intellectual refreshment which might be fairly exhausted in ten minute there remain nothing to beguile the hour but the perpetual stitch stitch stitch of an industriously - dispose sempstress ;  CHAPTER XLIV 

 after the FIRE 


 yes , it be marian . she whom Gilbert Fenton have seek so long and patiently , with doubt and anguish in his heart ; she whose double John Saltram have follow across the Atlantic , have be within easy reach of they all the time , hide away in that dreary old farm - house , the innocent victim of Percival Nowell 's treachery , and Stephen Whitelaw 's greed of gain . the whole story be tell by - and - by , when the master of Wyncomb Farm lie die .

"

 " yes , on the river - bank , within a short distance of Mr. Whitelaw 's house . he begin by congratulate I on the change in my prospect , I be a rich woman , he say . and then he go on to vilify my husband in such hateful word , Ellen ; tell I that I have marry a notorious scoundrel and profligate , and that he could produce ample evidence of what he affirm ; and all this with a pretended pity for my weakness and ignorance of the world . I laugh his shameful slander to scorn , and tell he that I know my husband too thoroughly to be alarm even for a moment by such groundless charge . he still affect to compassionate I as the weak and most credulous of woman , and then come to a proposal which he say he have travel to Hampshire on purpose to make to I . it be , that I should leave my husband , and place myself under his protection ; that I should go to America with he when he return there , and so preserve my fortune from the clutch of a villain . ' my fortune ? ' I say ; ' yes , I see that it be that alone you be think of . how can you suppose I so blind as not to understand that ? you have well be candid with I , and say frankly what you want . I have no doubt my husband will allow I to make any reasonable sacrifice in your favour . ' " 

 " what do he say to that ? " 

 " he laugh bitterly at my offer . ' your husband ! ' he say ' I be not likely to see the colour of my father 's money , if you be to be govern by he . ' ' you do he a great wrong , ' I answer . ' I be sure that he will act generously , and I shall be govern by he . ' " 

 " he be very angry , I suppose ? " 

 " no doubt of it ; but for some time he contrive to suppress all appearance of anger , and urge I to believe his statement about my husband , and to accept his offer of a home and protection with he . I want to get rid of he , he say , although this be likely to be our last interview the very last time in his life that he would ever see I , perhaps .  " the house have a strange empty look , I think . there be none of the life or bustle one expect to see at a farm ; all be silent as the grave . the gloom and quietness of the place chill I somehow . there be a fire burn in the parlour , and my father make I sit down very close to it , and I think the heat increase that faintness which I have feel when I come into the house . 

 " again and again he urge his first demand , seem as if he would wear down all opposition by persistence . I be quite firm ; but the effect of all this argument be very wearisome , and I begin to feel really ill .

's will . ' 

 " for a long time I sit like some stupid bewildered creature , go over these word again and again , as if I have no power to understand they . it be very long before I could believe that my father mean to shut I up in that room for an indefinite time for the rest of my life , perhaps . but , little by little , I come to believe this , and to feel nothing but a blank despair . o , Nelly , I dare not dwell upon that time ! I suffer too much . God have be very merciful to I in spar I my mind ; for there be time when I believe I be quite mad . I could pray sometimes , but not always . I have spend whole day in prayer , almost as if I fancy that I could weary out my God with supplication . " 

 " and Stephen ; do you see he ? " 

 " yes , now and then once in several day , in a week perhaps . he use to come , like the master of a madhouse visit his patient , to see that I be comfortable , he say . at first I use to appeal to he to set I free kneeling at his foot , promise any sacrifice of my fortune for he or for my father , if they would release I . but it be no use . he be as hard as a rock ; and at last I feel that it be useless , and use to see he come and go with hopeless apathy . no , Ellen , there be no word can describe what I suffer . I believe she really think I be a harmless madwoman , and that her master have a right to shut I up in that room . one night , after I have be there for a time that seem like eternity , my father come " 

 " what ! " cry Ellen Whitelaw , " the stranger ! I understand . that man be your father ; he come to see you that night ; and as he be leave you , you give that dreadful shriek we hear downstair . o , if I have know the truth if I have only know ! " 

 " you hear I , Ellen ? you be there ? " Marian exclaim , surprised . she be , as yet , entirely ignorant of Ellen 's marriage , and have be too much bewilder by the suddenness of her escape to wonder how the bailiff 's daughter have happen to be so near at hand in that hour of deadly peril .

I have have some experience of the result of oppose he , he say , and he now expect to find I reasonable .

Heaven know I would have give twenty year of my life to escape from that dismal place , with the mere chance of be able to get back to my husband ; but I would not take a false oath ; I could not perjure myself , as that man would have make I perjure myself , in order to win my release . I fancy afterwards that that cry must have be hear , and that , if there have be any creature in the house incline to help I , there would have come an end to my suffering . but the time pass , and there be no change ; only the long dreary day , the wretched sleepless night . " 

 this be all . there be detail of her suffering which Marian tell her faithful friend by - and - by , when her mind be calm , and they have leisure for tranquil talk ; but the story be all tell ; and Marian lie down to rest in the familiar room , unspeakably grateful to God for her rescue , and only eager that her husband should be inform of her safety . she have not yet be tell that he have cross the Atlantic in search of she , delude by a false scent . Ellen fear to tell she this at first ; and she have take it for grant that John Saltram be still in London . it be easy to defer any explanation just yet , on account of Marian 's weakness . the exertion of tell the brief story of her suffering have leave her prostrate ; and she be fain to obey her friendly nurse . 

 " we will talk about everything , and arrange everything , by - and - by , dear Mrs. Holbrook , " Ellen say resolutely ; " but for the present you must rest , and you must take everything that I bring you , and be very good . " 

 and with that she kiss and leave she , to perform another and less agreeable duty the duty of attendance by her husband 's sick - bed . 

 CHAPTER XLV 

 MR . WHITELAW make his will 


 they have carry Stephen Whitelaw to the Grange ; and he lie a helpless creature , beyond hope of recovery , in one of the roomy old - fashioned bed - chamber . 

 the humble Crosber surgeon have do his good , and have do it skilfully , be a man of large experience amongst a lowly class of sufferer ; and to the aid of the Crosber surgeon have come a more prosperous practitioner from Malsham , who have drive over in his own phaeton ; but between they both they could make nothing of Stephen Whitelaw . his race be run . he have be severely burn ; and if his actual injury be not enough to kill he , there be little chance that he could survive the shock which his system have receive . he might linger a little ; might hold out long than they expect ; but his life be a question of hour . 

 the doomed man have seem from the first to have a conviction of the truth , and appear in no manner surprised when , in answer to his question , the Malsham doctor admit that his case be fatal , and suggest that , if he have anything to do in the adjustment of his affair , he could scarcely do it too soon . at this Mr. Whitelaw groan aloud . if he could in any manner have adjust his affair so as to take his money with he , the suggestion might have seem sensible enough ; but , that be impracticable , it be the mere futility . he have never make a will ; it cost he too much anguish to give away his money even on paper . and now it be virtually necessary that he should do so , or else , perhaps , his wealth would , by some occult process , be seize upon by the crown a power which he have be accustom to regard in the abstract with an antagonistic feeling , as be the root of queen 's taxis . to leave all to his wife , with some slight pension to Mrs. Tadman , seem the most obvious course . he have marry for love , and the wife of his choice have be very dutiful and submissive . what more could he have demand from she ? and why should he grudge she the inheritance of his wealth ? well , he would not have grudge it to she , perhaps , since some one must have it , if it have not be for that aggravating conviction that she would marry again , and that the man she prefer to he would riot in the possession of his hardly - earn rich . she would marry Frank Randall ; and between they they would mismanage , and ultimately ruin , the farm . he remember the cost of the manure he have put upon his field that year , and regret that useless outlay . it be a hard thing to have enrich his land only that other might profit by the produce . 

 " and if I have   lay down a yard of drain - pipe since last year , I have   lay down a dozen mile . there be not a bit of swampy ground or a patch of sour grass on the farm , " he think bitterly . 

 he lie for some hour deliberate as to what he should do . death be near , but not so very close to he just yet . he have time to think . no , come what might , he would not leave the bulk of his property to fall into the keeping of Frank Randall . 

 he remember that there be charitable institution , to which a man , not wish to enrich an ungrateful race , might bequeath his money , and obtain some credit for himself thereby , which no man could expect from his own relation . there be an infirmary at Malsham , rather a juvenile institution as yet , in aid whereof Mr. Whitelaw have often be plague for subscription , reluctantly dole out half - a - guinea now and then , more often refuse to contribute anything . he have never think of this place in his life before ; but the image of it come into his mind now , as he have see it on market - day for the last four year a bran new red - brick building in Malsham high - street . he think how his name would look , cut in large letter on a stone tablet on the face of that edifice . it would be something to get for his money ; a very poor and paltry something , compare with the delight of possession , but just a little well than nothing . 

 he lie for some time ponder upon this , with that image of the stone tablet before his eye , set forth that the new wing of this institution have be erect at the desire of the late Stephen Whitelaw , Esq . , of Wyncomb Farm , who have bequeath a sum of money to the infirmary for that purpose , whereby two new ward have , in memory of that respected benefactor , be entitle the Whitelaw ward or something to the like effect . he compose a great many version of the inscription as he lie there , tolerably easy as to his bodily feeling , and chiefly anxious concern the disposal of the money ; but , be unaccustomed to the task of composition , he find it more difficult than he could have suppose to set forth his own glory in a concise form of word . but the tablet would be there , of course , the very centre and keystone of the building , as it be ; indeed , Mr. Whitelaw resolve to make his bequ contingent upon the fulfilment of this desire . later in the evening he tell William Carley that he have make up his mind about his will , and would be glad to see Mr. Pivott , of Malsham , rival solicitor to Mr. Randall , of the same town , as soon as that gentleman could be summon to his bedside . 

 the bailiff seem surprised at this request . 

 " why , surely , Steph , you can not   want a lawyer mix up in the business ! " he say . " those sort of chap only live by make work for one another . you know how to make your will well enough , old fellow , without any attorney 's aforesaid and hereinafter . half a sheet of paper and a couple of sentence would do it , I should think ; the few word the well . " 

 " I would rather have Pivott , and do it in a regular manner , " Mr. Whitelaw answer quietly . " I remember , in a forgery case that be in the paper the other day , how the judge say of the deceased testator , that , be a lawyer , he be too wise to make his own will . yes , I would rather see Pivott , if you will send for he , Carley . it be always good to be on the safe side . I do not   want my money waste in a chancery suit when I be lie in my grave . " 

 William Carley try to argue the matter with his son - in - law ; but the attempt be quite useless . Mr. Whitelaw have always be the most obstinate of man and lie on his bed , maim and helpless , be no more to be move from his resolve than if he have be a roman gladiator who have just train himself for an encounter with lion . so the bailiff be compel to obey he , unwillingly enough , and dispatch one of the man to Malsham in quest of Mr. Pivott the attorney . 

 the practitioner come to the Grange as fast as his horse could carry he . every one in Malsham know by this time that Stephen Whitelaw be a doomed man ; and Mr. Pivott feel that this be a matter of life and death . he be an eminently respectable man , plump and dapper , with a rosy smooth - shaven face , and an air of honesty that make the law seem quite a pleasant thing . he be speedily seat by Mr. Whitelaw 's bed , with a pair of candle and write material upon a little table before he , ready to obey his client 's behest , and with the self - possess aspect of a man to whom a last will and testament involve the disposal of a million or so would have be only an every - day piece of practice .

 " I think , Mr. Carley , it would be as well for our poor friend and I to be alone , " he say in his most courteous accent .

 " Steph , " say the bailiff abruptly , " do you want I out of the room ? say the word , if you do . " 

 the patient writhe , hesitate , and then reply with some confusion , 

 " if it be all the same to you , William Carley , I think I would soon be alone with Mr. Pivott . " 

 and here the polite attorney , have open the door with his own hand , bow the bailiff out ; and , to his extreme mortification , William Carley find himself on the outside of his son - in - law 's room , before he have time to make any farth remonstrance . 

 he go downstairs , and pace the wainscote parlour in a very savage frame of mind . 

 " there be some kind of devil 's work hatch up there , " he mutter to himself . " why should he want I out of the room ? he would not , if he be go to leave all his money to Ellen , as he ought to leave it . who else be there to get it ? not that old mother Tadman , surely . she be an artful old harridan ; and if my girl have not be a fool , she would have get rid of she out of hand when she marry . sure to goodness she can never stand between Stephen and his wife . and who else be there ? no one that I know of ; no one . Stephen would not   have keep any secret all these year from the folk he be live amongst . it be not   likely . he must leave it all to his wife , except a hundred or so , perhaps , to mother Tadman ; and it be nothing but his natural closeness that make he want I out of the way . " 

 and at this stage of his reflection , Mr. Carley open a cupboard near the fire - place and bring therefrom a case - bottle , from the content of which he find farth solace . it be about half - an - hour after this that he be summon by a call from the lawyer , who be stand on the broad landing - place at the top of the stair with a candle in his hand , when the bailiff emerge from the parlour . 

 " if you will step up here , and bring one of your man with you , I shall be oblige , Mr. Carley , " the attorney say , look over the banister ; " I want you to witness your son - in - law 's will . " Mr. Carley 's spirit rise a little at this . he be not much verse in the way of lawyer , and have a notion that Mr. Pivott would read the will to he , perhaps , before he sign it . it flash upon he presently that a legatee could not benefit by a will which he have witness . it be obvious , therefore , that Stephen do not mean he to have anything . well , he have scarcely expect anything . if his daughter inherit all , it would be pretty much the same thing ; she would act generously of course . 

 he go into the kitchen , where the head man , who have be retain on the premise to act as special messenger in this time of need , be sit in the chimney - corner smoke a comfortable pipe after his walk to and from Malsham . 

 " you be want upstairs a minute , Joe , " he say ; and the two go clumping up the wide old oaken staircase . 

 the witnessing of the will be a very brief business . Mr. Pivott do not offer to throw any light upon its content , nor be the bailiff , sharpsighte as he might be , able to seize upon so much as one paragraph or line of the document during the process of attach his signature thereto . 

 when the ceremony be conclude , Stephen Whitelaw sink back upon his pillow with an air of satisfaction . 

 " I do not   think I could have do any well , " he murmur . " it be a hard thing for a man of my age to leave everything behind he ; but I do not   see that I could have do well . " 

 " you have do that , my dear sir , which might afford comfort to any death - bed , " say the lawyer solemnly . 

 he fold the will , and put it into his pocket . 

 " our friend desire I to take charge of this document , " he say to William Carley . " you will have no reason to complain , on your daughter 's account , when you become familiar with its content . she have be fairly treat I may say very fairly treat . " 

 the bailiff do not much relish the tone of this assurance . fair treatment might mean very little . 

 " I hope she have be well treat , " he answer in a surly manner . " she be be a good wife to Stephen Whitelaw , and would continue so to be if he be to live twenty year long . when a pretty young woman marry a man twice her age , she be a right to expect handsome treatment , Mr. Pivott . it can not   be too handsome for justice , in my opinion . " 

 the solicitor give a little gentle sigh . 

 " as an interested party , Mr. Carley , " he say , " your opinion be not as valuable as it might be under other circumstance . however , I do not   think your daughter will complain , and I be sure the world will applaud what our poor friend have do of his own accord , mind , Mr. Carley , wholly and solely of his own spontaneous desire . it be a thing that I should only have be too proud to suggest ; but the responsibility of such a suggestion be one which I could never have take upon myself . it would have be out of my province , indeed . you will be kind enough to remember this by - and - by , my dear sir . " 

 the bailiff be puzzle , and show Mr. Pivott to the door with a moody countenance . 

 " I think there be some devil 's work , " he mutter to himself , as he watch the lawyer mount his stiff brown cob and ride away into the night ; " but what do it all mean ? and what have Stephen Whitelaw do with his money ? we shall know that pretty soon , anyhow . he can not   last long . " 

 CHAPTER XLVI 

 ellen regain her liberty 


 Stephen Whitelaw linger for two day and two night , and at the expiration of that time depart this life , make a very decent end of it , and trouble by no thought that his existence have be an unworthy one . 

 before he die , he tell his wife something of how he have be tempt into the doing of that foul deed whereof Marian Saltram have be the victim . those two be alone together the day before he die , when Stephen , of his own free will , make the follow statement : 

 " it be Mrs. Holbrook 's father , you see , " he say , in a plausible tone , " that put it to I , how he might want his daughter take care of for a time it might be a short time , or it might be rather a longish time , accord to how circumstance should work out . we have meet once before at the King 's arm at Malsham , where Mr. Nowell be stay , and where I go in of an evening , once in a way , after market ; and he would make pretty free with I , and ask I a good many question about myself , and tell I a good bit about himself , in a friendly way . he tell I how his daughter have go against he , and be likely to go against he , and how some property that ought in common justice to have be leave to he , have be leave to she . he be go to give she a fair chance , he say , if she like to leave her husband , who be a scheming scoundrel , and obey he . she might have a happy home with he , if she be reasonable . if not , he should use his authority as a father .

 " well , you see , Nell , as he seem to have take a fancy to I , as you may say , and have tell I he could put I up to make more of my money , and have altogether be uncommonly pleasant , I do not   care to say no , and I go . I be rather take aback at the King 's arm when they show I to a private room , because I have meet Mr. Nowell before in the Commercial ; however , there he be , sit in front of a blaze fire , and with a couple of decanter of wine upon the table . 

 " he be very civil , could not   have be more friendly , and we talk and talk ; he be always harp on his daughter ; till at last he come out with what he want . would I give her house - room for a bit , just to keep she out of the way of her husband and such - like design people , suppose she should turn obstinate and refuse to go abroad with he ? ' " 

 " o , Stephen ! " cry his wife reproachfully , " how could you ever consent to such a wicked thing ? " 

 " I do not   know about the wickedness of it , " Mr. Whitelaw respond , with rather a sullen air ; " a daughter be bind to obey her father , be not   she ? and if she do not , I should think he have the power to do what he like with she . that be how I should look at it , if I be a father . it be all very well to talk , you see , Nell , but you do not   know the argument such a man as that can bring to bear . I do not   want to do it ; I be against it from the first . it be a dangerous business , and might bring I into trouble . but that man bear down upon I to that extent that he make I promise anything ; and when I go home that night , it be with the understanding that I be to fit up a room there be a double door to be put up to shut out sound , and a deal more ready for Mrs. Holbrook , in case her father want to get she out of the way for a bit . " 

 " he promise to pay you , of course ? " Ellen say , not quite able to conceal the contempt and aversion which this confession of her husband 's inspire . 

 " well , yes , a man do not   put himself in jeopardy like that for nothing . he be to give I a certain sum of money down the first night that Mrs. Holbrook sleep in my house ; and another sum of money before he go to America , and an annual sum for continue to take care of she , if he want to keep she quiet permanently , as he might . altogether it would be a very profitable business , he tell I , and I ought to consider myself uncommonly lucky to get such a chance . as to the kindness or unkindness of the matter , it be well than shut she up in a lunatic asylum , he say ; and he might have to do that , if I refuse to take she . she be very weak in her head , he say , and the doctor would throw no difficulty in his way , if he want to put she into a madhouse . " 

 " but you must have know that be a lie ! " exclaim Ellen indignantly . " you have see and talk to she ; you must have know that Mrs. Holbrook be as sane as you or i. " 

 " I could not   be suppose to know well than her own father , " answer Mr. Whitelaw , in an injure tone ; " he have a right to know well . however , it be no use argue about it now . he have such a power over I that I could not   go against he ; so I give in , and Mrs. Holbrook come to Wyncomb . she be to be treat kindly and make comfortable , her father say ; that be agree between we ; and she have be treat kindly and make comfortable . I have to trust some one to wait upon she , and when Mr. Nowell see the two girl he choose Sarah Batts . ' that girl will do anything for money , ' he say ; ' she be stupid , but she be wise enough to know her own interest , and she will hold her tongue . ' so I trust Sarah Batts , and I have to pay she pretty stiffly to keep the secret ; but she be a rare one to do the work , and she go about it as quiet as a mouse . not even mother Tadman ever suspect she . " 

 " it be a wicked piece of business wicke from first to last , " say Ellen . " I can not   bear to hear about it . " 

 and then , remember that the sinner be so near his end , and that this voluntary confession of his be in some manner a sign of repentance , she feel some compunction , and speak to he in a soft tone . 

 " still I be grateful to you for tell I the truth at last , Stephen , " she say ; " and , thank God , there be no harm do that need last for ever . thank God that dear young lady do not lose her life , shut up a prisoner in that miserable room , as she might have do . " 

 " she have her victual regular , " observe Mr. Whitelaw , " and the good . " 

 " eat and drinking will not   keep any one alive , if their heart 's breaking , " say Ellen ; " but , thank heaven , her suffering have come to an end now , and I trust God will forgive your share in they , Stephen . " 

 and then , sit by his bedside through the long hour of that night , she try in very simple word to awaken he to a sense of his condition . it be not an easy business to let any glimmer of spiritual light in upon the darkness of that sordid mind . there do arise perhaps in this last extremity some dim sense of remorse in the breast of Mr. Whitelaw , some vague consciousness that in that one act of his life , and in the whole tenor of his life , he have not exactly shape his conduct accord to that model which the parson have hold up for his imitation in certain rather prosy sermon , indifferently hear , on the rare occasion of his attendance at the parish church . but whatever terror the world to come might hold for he seem very faint and shapeless , compare with the thing from which he be to be take . he think of his untimely death as a hardship , an injustice almost . when his wife entreat he to see the vicar of Crosber before he die , he refuse at first , ask what good the vicar 's talk could do he . 

 " if he could keep I alive as long as till next July , to see how those turnip answer with the new dressing , I would see he fast enough , " he say peevishly ; " but he can not ; and I do not   want to hear his preaching . " 

 " but it would be a comfort to you , surely , Stephen , to have he talk to you a little about the goodness and mercy of God . he will not   tell you hard thing , I be sure of that . " 

 " no , I suppose he will try and make believe that death 's uncommon pleasant , " answer Mr. Whitelaw with a bitter laugh ; " as if it could be pleasant to any man to leave such a place as Wyncomb , after do as much for the land , and spending as much labour and money upon it , as I have do . it be like nurse tell child that a dose of physic 's pleasant ; they would not   like to have to take it themselves . " 

 and then by - and - by , when his last day have dawn , and he feel himself grow weak , Mr. Whitelaw express himself willing to comply with his wife 's request . 

 " if it be any satisfaction to you , Nell , I will see the parson , " he say . " his talk can not   do I much harm , anyhow . " whereupon the rector of Crosber and Hallibury be send for , and come swiftly to perform his duty to the die man . he be closet with Mr. Whitelaw for some time , and do his good to awaken christian feeling in the farmer 's breast ; but it be doubtful if his pious effort result in much . the soul of Stephen Whitelaw be in his barn and granary , with his pig and cattle . he could not so much as conceive the idea of a world in which there should be no such thing as sale and profit . 

 his end come quietly enough at last , and Ellen be free . her time of bondage have be very brief , yet she feel herself twenty year old than she have seem before that interval of misery begin . 

 when the will be read by Mr. Pivott on the day of Stephen Whitelaw 's funeral , it be find that the farmer have leave his wife two hundred a year , derivable from real estate . to Mrs. Rebecca Tadman , his cousin , he bequeath an annuity of forty pound , the say annuity to revert to Ellen upon Mrs. Tadman 's death should Ellen survive . the remain portion of his real estate he bequeath to one John James Harris , a distant cousin , who own a farm in Wiltshire , with whom Stephen Whitelaw have spend some year of his boyhood , and from whom he have learn the science of agriculture . it be less from any love the testator bear John James Harris than from a morbid jealousy of his probable successor Frank Randall , that the Wiltshire farmer have be name as residuary legatee . if Stephen Whitelaw could have leave his real estate to the Infirmary , he would have so leave it . his personal estate , consist of diver investment in railway share and other kind of stock , all of a very safe kind , be to be realize , and the entire proceed devote to the erection of an additional wing for the extension of Malsham Infirmary , and his gift be to be record on a stone tablet in a conspicuous position on the front of that building . this , which be an absolute condition attach to the bequest , have be set forth with great minuteness by the lawyer , at the special desire of his client . 

 Mr. Carley 's expression of opinion after hear this will read need not be record here . it be forcible , to say the least of it ; and Mr. Pivott , the Malsham solicitor , protest against such language as an outrage upon the fine feeling of our nature . 

 " some degree of disappointment be perhaps excusable upon your part , my dear sir , " say the lawyer , who wish to keep the widow for his client , and have therefore no desire to offend her father ; " but I be sure that in your calm moment you will admit that the work to which your son - in - law have devote the bulk of his accumulation be a noble one . for age to come the sick and the suffering among our townsfolk will bless the name of Whitelaw . there be a touching reflection for you , Mr. Carley ! and really now , your amiable daughter , with an income of two hundred per annum to say nothing of that reversion which must fall in to she by - and - by on Mrs. Tadman 's decease be leave in a very fair position . I should not have consent to draw up that will , sir , if I have consider it an unjust one . " 

 " then there be a wide difference between your notion of justice and mine , " growl the bailiff ; who thereupon relapse into grim silence , feel that complaint be useless . he could no more alter the condition of Mr. Whitelaw 's will than he could bring Mr. Whitelaw back to life and that last operation be one which he be by no mean eager to perform . 

 Ellen herself feel no disappointment ; she fancy , indeed , that her husband , whom she have never deceive by any pretence of affection , have behave with sufficient generosity towards she . two hundred a year seem a large income to she . it would give her perfect independence , and the power to help other , if need be . 

 CHAPTER XLVII 

 CLOSING SCENES 


 it be not until the day of her husband 's funeral that Ellen Whitelaw write to Mr. Fenton to tell he what have happen . she know that her letter be likely to bring he post - haste to the Grange , and she wish his come to be defer until that last dismal day be over . nor be she sorry that there should be some little pause a brief interval of ignorance and tranquillity in Marian 's life before she hear of her husband 's useless voyage across the Atlantic . she be in sad need of rest of mind and body , and even in those few day gain considerable strength , by the aid of Mrs. Whitelaw 's tender nursing . she have not leave her room during the time that death be in the darken house , and it be only on the morning after the funeral that she come downstairs for the first time . her appearance have improve wonderfully in that interval of little more than a week . her eye have lose their dim weary look , the deathly pallor of her complexion have give place to a faint bloom . but grateful as she be for her own deliverance , she be full of anxiety about her husband . Ellen Whitelaw 's vague assurance that all would be well , that he would soon be restore to she , be not enough to set her mind at ease . 

 Ellen have not the courage to tell she the truth . it be well that Gilbert Fenton should do that , she think . he who know all the circumstance of Mr. Holbrook 's journey , and the probability as to his return , would be so much well able to comfort and reassure his wife . 

 " he will come to - day , I have no doubt , " Ellen say to herself on the morning after her husband 's funeral . 

 she tell Marian how she have write to Mr. Fenton on the day before , in order to avoid the agitation of a surprise , should he appear at the Grange without wait to announce his coming . nor be she mistake as to the probability of his speedy arrival . it be not long after noon when there come a loud peal of the bell that ring so rarely . Ellen run herself to the gate to admit the visitor . she have tell he of her husband 's death in her last letter , and her widow 's weed be no surprise to he . he be pale , but very calm . 

 " she be well ? " he ask eagerly . 

 " yes , sir , she be as well as one could look for she to be , poor dear , after what she have go through . but she be much change since last you see she . you must prepare yourself for that , sir . and she be very anxious about her husband . I do not   know how she will take it , when she hear that he have go to America . " 

 " yes , that be a bad business , Mrs. Whitelaw , " Gilbert answer gravely . " he be not in a fit state to travel , unfortunately . he be only just recover from a severe illness , and be as weak as a child . " 

 " o dear , o dear ! but you will not   tell Mrs. Holbrook that , sir ? " 

 " I will not   tell she more than I can help ; of course I do not   want to alarm she ; but I be bind to tell she some portion of the truth . you do her husband a great wrong , you see , Mrs. Whitelaw , when you suspect he of some share in this vile business . he have show himself really devoted to she . I thank God that it have prove so . and now tell I more about this affair ; your letter explain so little . " 

 " I will tell you all , sir . " 

 they walk in the garden for about a quarter of an hour before Gilbert go into the house . Eager as he be to see Marian , he be still more anxious to hear full particular of that foul plot of which she have be make the victim . Ellen Whitelaw tell he the story very plainly , make no attempt to conceal her husband 's guilty part in the business ; and the story be finish , she take he straight to the parlour where he have see Marian for the first time after her marriage . 

 it be a warm bright day , and all three window be open . Marian be sit by one of they , with some scrap of work lie forget in her lap . she start up from her seat as Gilbert go into the room , and hasten forward to meet he . 

 " how good of you to come ! " she cry . " and you have bring I news of my husband ? I be sure of that . " 

 " yes , dear Mrs. Holbrook Mrs. Saltram ; may I not call you by that name now ? I know all ; and have forgive all . " 

 " then you know how deeply he sin against you , and how much he value your friendship ? he would never have play so false a part but for that . he could not bear to think of be estranged from you . " 

 " we be not estranged . I have try to be angry with he ; but there be some old tie that a man can not break . he have use I very ill , Marian ; but he be still my friend . " 

 his voice break a little as he utter the old familiar name . yes , she be change , cruelly change , by that ordeal of six month ' suffering . the brightness of her beauty have quite fade ; but there be something in the altered face that touch he more deeply than the old magic . she be dearer to he , perhaps , in this hour than she have ever be yet . Dearer to he , and yet divide from he utterly , now that he profess himself her husband 's friend as well as her own . 

 friendship , brotherly affection , those chasten sentiment which he have fancy have supersede all warm feeling where be they now ? by the passionate beating of his heart , by his eager longing to clasp that fade form to his breast , he know that he love she as dearly as on the day when she promise to be his wife ; that he must love she with the same measure till the end of his existence . 

 " thank God for that , " Marian say gently ; " thank God that you be still friend . but why do he not come with you to - day ? you have tell he about I , I suppose ? " 

 " not yet , Marian ; I have not be able to do that . nor could he come with I to - day . he have leave England on a false scent . " 

 and then he tell she , in a few word , the story of John Saltram 's voyage to New York ; make very light of the matter , and speak cheerily of his early return . 

 " he will come back at once , of course , when he find how he have be deceive , " Gilbert say . 

 Marian be cruelly distress by this disappointment . she try to bear the blow bravely , and listen with a gentle patience to Gilbert 's reassure argument ; but it be a hard thing to bear . 

 " he will be back soon , you say , " she say ; " but soon be such a vague word ; and you have not tell I when he go . " 

 Gilbert tell she the date of John Saltram 's departure . she begin immediately to question he as to the usual length of the voyage , and to calculate the time he have have for his going and return . take the average length of the voyage as ten day , and allow ten day for delay in New York , a month would give ample time for the two journey ; and John Saltram have be away more than a month . 

 Gilbert could see that Marian be quick to take alarm on discover this . 

 " my dear Mrs. Saltram , be reasonable , " he say gently . " find such a cheat put upon he , your husband would naturally be anxious to bring your father to some kind of reckoning , to extort from he the real secret of your fate . he would no doubt stay in New York to do this ; and we can not tell how difficult the business might prove , or how long it would occupy he . " 

 " but if he have be detain like that , he would surely have write to you , " say Marian ; " and you have hear nothing from he since he leave England . " 

 " unhappily nothing . but he be not the good correspondent in the world , you know . " 

 " yes , yes , I know that . yet , in such a case as this , he would surely have write , if he be well . " her eye meet Gilbert 's as she say this . she stop abruptly , dismay by something in his face .

 he have not mean to admit even as much as this just yet ; but have say this , he find himself compel to say more . Marian question he so closely , that she finally extort from he the whole history of John Saltram 's illness . after that it be quite in vain to attempt consolation . she be very gentle , very patient , trouble he with no vain wailing and lamentation ; but he could see that her heart be almost broken . 

 he leave she at the end of a few hour to return to London , promise to go on to Liverpool next day , in order to be on the spot to await her husband 's return , and to send she the early possible tiding of it . 

 " your friendship for we have give you nothing but trouble and pain , " she say ; " but if you will do this for I , I shall be grateful to you for the rest of my life . " 

 there be no occasion for that journey to Liverpool . when he arrive in London that night , Gilbert Fenton find a letter wait for he at his Wigmore - street lodging a letter with the New York post - mark , but not address in his friend 's hand . he tear it open hurriedly , just a little alarmed by this fact .

 " my dear Gilbert , " he write , " I have be dupe . this man Nowell be a most consummate scoundrel . the woman with he be not marian , but some girl whom he have pick up to represent she his wife perhaps , or something bad . I be very ill on the passage out , and only discover the trick at the last . since then I have trace the scoundrel to his quarter , and have have an interview with he rather a stormy one , as you may suppose . but the long and short of it be that he defy I . he tell I that my wife be in England , and safe , but will admit no more . I have consult a lawyer here , but it seem I can do nothing against he or nothing that will not involve a more complicated and protract business than I have time or patience for . I do not   want this wretch to go scot - free . it be evident that he have hatch this plot in order to get possession of his daughter 's money , and I have little doubt the lawyer Medler be in it . but of course my first duty , as well as my most ardent desire , be to find Marian ; and for this purpose I shall come back to England by the first steamer that will convey I , leave Mr. Nowell 's punishment to the chance of the future . my dear girl 's property , as well as herself , will be well protect by my presence in England . " 

 there be a pause here , and the next paragraph be date two day after . 

 " if I have strength to come , I shall return by the next steamer ; but the fact be , my dear Gilbert , I be very ill have be completely prostrate since write the above and a doctor here tell I I must not think of the voyage yet awhile . but I shall not   allow his opinion to govern I . if I can crawl to the steamer , which start three day hence , I shall come . " 

 then there be another break , and again the writer go on in a weak and more straggling hand , without any date this time . 

 " my dear Gil , it be nearly a week since I write the last line , and I have   be in bed ever since . I be afraid there be no hope for I ; in plain word , I believe I be die . to you I leave the duty I be not allow to perform . Marian be live , and in England . I believe that scoundrelly father of hers tell I the truth when he declare that . you will not rest till you find she , I know ; and you will protect her fortune from that wretch . God bless you , faithful old friend ! Heaven know how I yearn for the sight of your honest face , lie here among stranger , to be bury in a foreign land . see that my wife pay Mrs. Branston the money I borrow to come here ; and tell she that I be grateful to she , and think of she on my die bed . to my wife I send no message . she know that I love she ; but how dear she have be to I in this bitter time of separation , she can never know . 

 " you will find a bulky MS . at my chamber , in the bottom drawer on the right side of my desk . it be my life of Swift unfinishe as my own life . if , after read it , you should think it worth publish , as a fragment , with my name to it , I should wish you to arrange its publication . I should be glad to leave my name upon something . " 

 in a stranger 's hand , and upon another sheet of paper , Gilbert read the end of his friend 's history . 

 " Sir , I regret to inform you that your friend Mr. Saltram expire at eleven o'clock last night   Wednesday , May 2nd , after an illness of a fortnight 's duration , throughout which I give he my good attention as his medical adviser . he will be bury in the Cypress - hill Cemetery , on Long Island , at his own request ; and he have leave sufficient fund for the necessary expense , and the payment of his hotel bill , as well as my own small claim against he . any surplus which may be leave I shall forward to you , when these payment have be make . I enclose a detailed account of the case for your satisfaction , and have the honour to be , sir , 

 " your very obediently , 

 " SILAS WARREN , M.D. 

 " 113 sixteenth - street , New York , 

 " May 3 , 186 . " 

 this be all . 

 and Gilbert have to carry these tiding to Marian . for a time he be almost paralyze by the blow . he have love this man as a brother ; if he have ever doubt the strength of his attachment to John Saltram , he know it now . but the bad of all be , that one bitter fact Marian must be tell , and by he . 

 he go back to the Grange next day . again and again upon that miserable journey he act over the scene which be to take place when he come to the end of it in spite of himself , as it be go over the word he be to say , while Marian 's face rise before he like a picture . how be he to tell she ? would not the very fact of this desolation come to she from his lip be sufficient to make he hateful to she in all the day to come ? More than once upon that journey he be tempt to turn back , and to leave his dismal news to be tell in a letter . 

 but when the fatal moment do at last arrive , the event in no manner realize the picture of his imagination . time be not give to he to speak those solemn preliminary word by which he have intend to prepare the victim for her deathblow . his presence there , and his presence alone , be all sufficient to prepare she for some calamity . 

 " you have come back to I , and without he ! " she exclaim . " tell I what have happen ; tell I at once . " 

 he have no time to defer the stroke . his face tell she so much . in a few moment before his broken word could shape themselves into coherence she know all . 

 there be some thing that can never be forget . never , to his die day , can Gilbert Fenton forget the quiet agony he have to witness then . 

 she be very ill for a long time after that day in danger of death . all that she have suffer during her confinement at Wyncomb seem to fall upon she now with a double weight . only the supreme devotion of those who care for she could have carry she through that weary time ; but the day do at last come when the peril be pronounce a thing of the past , and the feeble submissive patient might be carry away from the Grange from the scene of her brief married life and of her bitter widowhood . 

 she go with Ellen Whitelaw to Ventnor . it be late in August before she be able to bear this journey ; and in this mild refuge for invalid she remain throughout the winter . 

 even during that trying time , when it seem more than doubtful whether she could live to profit by her grandfather 's bequest , her interest have be carefully watch by Gilbert Fenton . it be tolerably evident to his mind that Mr. Medler have be a tacit accomplice in Percival Nowell 's fraud ; or , at any rate , that he have enable the pretended Mrs. Holbrook to obtain a large sum of ready money with great ease than she could have do have he , as executor , be scrupulously careful to obtain her identification from some more trustworthy person than he know Percival Nowell to be . 

 whether these suspicion of Gilbert 's be correct , whether the lawyer have be actually deceive , or have willingly lend himself to the furtherance of Nowell 's design , must remain unascertained ; as well as the amount of profit which Mr. Medler may have secure to himself by the transaction . the law hold he liable for the whole of the money thus pay over in fraud or error ; but the law could do very little against a man whose sole earthly possession appear to be comprise by the worm - eat desk and shabby chair and table in his dingy office . the poor consolation remain of make an attempt to get he strike off " the Rolls ; " but when the City firm of solicitor in whose hand Gilbert have place Mrs. Saltram 's affair suggest this , Marian herself entreat that the man might have the benefit of the doubt as to his complicity with her father , and that no effort should be make to bring legal ruin upon he . 

 " there have be enough misery cause by this money already , " she say . " let the matter rest . I be rich than I care to be , as it be . " 

 of course Mr. Medler be not allow to retain his position as executor . the Court of Chancery be appeal to in the usual manner , and intervene for the future protection of Mrs. Saltram 's interest . 

 about Nowell 's conduct there be , of course , no doubt ; but after waste a good deal of money and trouble in his pursuit , Gilbert be fain to abandon all hope of catch he in the wide region of the new world . it be ascertain that the woman who have accompany he in the Orinoco as his daughter be actually his wife a girl whom he have meet at some low London dancing - room , and marry within a fortnight of his introduction to she . it be possible that prudence as well as attachment may have have something to do with this alliance . Mr. Nowell know that , once unite to he in the bond of holy matrimony , the accomplice of his fraud would have no power to give evidence against he . the amount which he have contrive to secure to himself by this plot amount in all to something under four thousand pound ; and out of this it may fairly be suppose that Mr. Medler claim a considerable percentage . the only information that Gilbert Fenton could ever obtain from America be , of a shabby swindler arrest in a gambling - house in one of the more remote western city , whose description correspond pretty closely with that of Marian 's father . 

 there come a time for the healing of all grief . the cruel wound close at last , though the scar , and the bitter memory of the stroke , may remain for ever . there come a time some year after John Saltram 's death when Gilbert Fenton have his reward . and if the woman he win for his wife in these latter day be not quite the fresh young beauty he have woo under the walnut - tree in Captain Sedgewick 's garden , she be still infinitely more beautiful than all other woman in his eye ; she be still the dearest and good and bright and purest of all earthly creature for he . in that happy time that perfect summer and harvest of his life all his fond dream have be realize . he have the home he so often picture , the child whose airy voice sound in his dream , the dear face always near he , and , sweet than all , the knowledge that he be love almost as he love . the bitter apprenticeship have be serve , and the full reward have be grant . 

 for Ellen Whitelaw too have come the period of compensation , and the farmer 's bad fear have be realize as to Frank Randall 's participation in that money he love so well . the income grudgingly leave to his wife by Stephen have enable Mr. Randall to begin business as a solicitor upon his own account , in a small town near London , with every apparent prospect of success . Ellen 's home be within easy reach of the river - side villa occupy by Mr. and Mrs. Fenton ; so she be able to see her dear Marian as often as she like ; nor be there any guest at the villa more welcome than this faithful friend . 

 the half - write memoir of Jonathan Swift be publish ; and reviewer , who have no compunction in praise the dead , be quick to recognize the touch of a master hand , the trenchant style of a powerful thinker . for the public the book be of no great value ; it be merely a curiosity of literature ; but it be the only monument of his own rugged genius which bear the name of John Saltram . 

 poor little Mrs. Branston have not sacrifice all the joy of life to the mane of her faithless lover . she be now the happy wife of a dash naval officer , and give pleasant party which bring life and light into the great house in Cavendish - square ; party to which Theobald Pallinson come , and where he shin as a small feeble star when great light be absent sing his last little song , or recite his last little poem , for the delight of some small coterie of single lady not in the first bloom of youth ; but party from which Mrs. Pallinson keep aloof in a stern spirit of condemnation , inform she choose familiar that she be never more cruelly deceive than in that misguided ungrateful young woman , Adela Branston .
